  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_36ca2d29-d211-4618-88f7-93cec37e3a56'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };

  <span id="freeText12132473976237313547" style="display:none">17-year-old Kate has lived her whole life in abject poverty, with an alcoholic father and drug-addicted mother, who severely abuses Kate. At school, her second-hand clothing marks her as a target. Her refusal to stand up for herself makes her the recipient of her classmates taunts and bullying. That is, until Henry returns. <br /><br />Henry Jamison moved away six years earlier, just as he and Kate had begun to develop feelings for one another. He returns to find the bright, funny, outgoing girl he had known now timidly hiding in corners, barely speaking to anyone around her, suspicious of even him. <br /><br />Kate can't figure out what game Henry is playing with her - for surely it is a game. What else would the gorgeous, popular boy from her past want with her? <br /><br />Kate finally decides to trust Henry's intentions, opening her heart to him. Just when it seems he might be genuine in his friendship, tragedy strikes, threatening everything Kate has worked so hard to gain. Can Henry help her to overcome this new devastation, or will it tear them apart forever?</span>

  <div class="friendReviews elementListBrown" >
    <div class="section firstReview">
      

<div id="review_215325675" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/215325675" />
    <a title="Alex" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1861778-alex"><img alt="Alex" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1415574136p2/1861778.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/215325675?book_show_action=true">Sep 26, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Alex" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Alex" href="/user/show/1861778-alex">Alex</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1861778-alex?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1861778-alex?shelf=kindle">kindle</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1861778-alex?shelf=really-terrible">really-terrible</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer215325675&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer215325675" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15585593465009268510">What the fuck? I cannot understand how people are giving it 5-star reviews because this was one of the worst things I've ever read.<br/><br/>I couldn't believe the whole book was so black and white. Kate, a victim of horrible abuse at the hands of her mother, has been ridiculed by her peers for her appearance for years. In fact, they physically abuse her too (wtf that scene)! But her knight on a white horse comes to her rescue in the form of Henry, her friend from childhood who has recently moved back to </span>
  <span id="freeText15585593465009268510" style="display:none">What the fuck? I cannot understand how people are giving it 5-star reviews because this was one of the worst things I've ever read.<br /><br />I couldn't believe the whole book was so black and white. Kate, a victim of horrible abuse at the hands of her mother, has been ridiculed by her peers for her appearance for years. In fact, they physically abuse her too (wtf that scene)! But her knight on a white horse comes to her rescue in the form of Henry, her friend from childhood who has recently moved back to town. Henry is The Perfect Man. He's rich, kind, generous, and has loved Kate ever since they were little...even though he moved away.<br /><br />Henry finds Kate irresistible. In fact, we are told that Kate's beauty is what her peers, especially the girls, hate about her. It Cannot Be Diminished By Her Circumstances. Henry has no problem getting Kate to fall in love with him, though she refuses to tell him about her home life. Which, in all fairness, is really really horrible.<br /><br />But the whole thing was gross. Kate had no autonomy. Henry saved her. He swooped in and literally is her salvation. She isn't able to do anything without him. Also, everyone loves Kate. Everyone who matters, that is. Which is Henry and his whole wonderful family. THEY LOVE HER IMMEDIATELY. THEY ARE THE PERFECT FAMILY. HIS MOTHER MAKES PUMPKIN SOUP AND SERVES IT IN HOLLOW PUMPKINS. HIS GRANDFATHER GIVES HER $1000 SIMPLY BECAUSE HE CAN SEE THAT SHE IS HENRY'S SOULMATE.<br /><br />And why? I don't know. Kate is always telling herself that she doesn't deserve him and he's too good for her and, well, he's her only friend. GROSS. This story could have totally set Kate up as an awesome female protagonist, doing the best despite her circumstances, and using her own tools to love Henry AND to escape her abuse, but instead it's Henry who does everything for her. I mean, don't men always?<br /><br />Henry even proposes at the end, even though they're 17. I don't know what 13-year-old wrote this book, but it was atrocious. It's some pathetic fantasy concocted out of soap opera-worthy melodrama, written by a woman who clearly believes that only men can save battered women. I had trouble believing that this book actually existed and that I was reading it. But, you know, why shouldn't it be? Millions of idiots love Twilight; why shouldn't they also love this piece of trash?<br /><br />EDIT: The more I think about this book, the more upset I am. I actually think this is one of those novels doing a disservice to young women living with domestic violence because it tells them that only a man can come save them. This will make it far more likely for these young women to go from one abusive situation into another one, becoming emotionally dependent on their "savior", and unable to develop their independence. For example, Kate, who leaves her mother only to go to Henry.<br /><br />(Let's not even go into Kate's mother's depression and mental illness, which is an incredibly sad story in itself...)<br /><br />This isn't to say that Henry isn't a paragon of virtue, because apparently he's the Greatest Dude Ever. Which is awesome for Kate and all, since that really could've ended poorly. But Bennett could have easily EASILY made Kate the hero of her own story. I know I'm getting all rah-rah feminist (WHICH I HAPPEN TO THINK IS GREAT), but honestly, I saw this kind of stuff every day with my young female clients. <br /><br />That being said, this thing was just crock full of shit. I apparently forgot to address the part where the Mean Girl bully beats the crap out of Kate at school. Like, physically, on the floor of the girls' bathroom, beats the crap out of her. It's needlessly violent and gratuitous. But once the truth about Kate's home life is revealed, suddenly the bully is all apologetic and weepy. Like, "SORRY FOR BEATING YOU UP. I THOUGHT YOU WERE ALL GROSS AND SMELLY AND STUFF. I TOTES WOULDN'T HAVE DONE THAT IF I KNEW YOU WERE GETTING BEATEN ON AT HOME. MY B." And Kate's all, "NBD, girl, I got you."<br /><br />YEAH.<br /><br />THAT HAPPENS.<br /><br />AND THEN THEY BECOME FRIENDS.<br /><br />So...what's the message I'm getting here? That it was okay for her to beat Kate up had Kate NOT been from an abusive home? Or, maybe, and I'm going out on a limb here, Bennett could have made it clear that such bullying and violence is abhorrent under ANY circumstance. I'm not saying that Bennett was condoning the physical and emotional bullying by justifying it like that. I'm saying that was how it read in the book and I just wish that Jessica (was that her name?) could have undergone her own transformation in a different way as well.<br /><br />In conclusion: if you're a sane person with rational ideas about how people should treat each other and you like strong female characters, you're probs going to want to throw your ebook reader against the wall. I wish I could give this NEGATIVE STARS. I know I shouldn't expect YA authors to be role models, BUT THEY ARE, because youth read their books and are influenced by them and TAKE THEM TO HEART. And that's why books like this and Twilight INFURIATE me. At least Henry doesn't creep into Kate's bedroom to watch her sleep. We should be telling young women that THEY ARE STRONG AND THEY ARE THE PROTAGONISTS OF THEIR OWN STORY AND THEY SHOULD NEVER UNDERESTIMATE THEMSELVES. We should never, ever tell them that they can only be someone in relation to someone else.<br /><br />THE END FOR REALZ.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15585593465009268510" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_209579862" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/209579862" />
    <a title="Sita" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5831199-sita"><img alt="Sita" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1506310723p2/5831199.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/209579862?book_show_action=true">Sep 16, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sita" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sita" href="/user/show/5831199-sita">Sita</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5831199-sita?shelf=own">own</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5831199-sita?shelf=favourites">favourites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5831199-sita?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5831199-sita?shelf=teen-romance">teen-romance</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer209579862" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9434323796834926419">Heart on a chain is such a beautiful book, let me just start by saying that I rarely ever cry during books. I cried reading <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/39999.The_Boy_in_the_Striped_Pajamas' title='The Boy in the Striped Pajamas by John Boyne' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Boy in the Striped Pajamas</a> and that was about it. I am not saying that I never cry. I cry. I cried watching despicable me, for goodness sake. I saw it in the theatres and my friend was silently laughing while these silent tears rolled down my cheeks. I went into a hysterical fit while watching Bambi and Dumbo.<br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380359110i/710272.jpg' width='200' height='160' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/> I even laugh so hard I cry at the dinner table; yep I’m a cr</span>
  <span id="freeText9434323796834926419" style="display:none">Heart on a chain is such a beautiful book, let me just start by saying that I rarely ever cry during books. I cried reading <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/39999.The_Boy_in_the_Striped_Pajamas" title="The Boy in the Striped Pajamas by John Boyne" rel="nofollow noopener">The Boy in the Striped Pajamas</a> and that was about it. I am not saying that I never cry. I cry. I cried watching despicable me, for goodness sake. I saw it in the theatres and my friend was silently laughing while these silent tears rolled down my cheeks. I went into a hysterical fit while watching Bambi and Dumbo.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380359110i/710272.jpg" width="200" height="160" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br> I even laugh so hard I cry at the dinner table; yep I’m a cryer. But for some reason, I rarely ever cry during a book, so to bring so much emotion from me (a crying but not crying person), has to be an achievement.<br><br>What can I say? This book was amazing, it was everything a good book should be, it was heart-warming, it had amazing (not all good) characters, it had an amazing hero and heroine, it had a great plot and it was really well written. What can I say? I loved it. Because I am terrible at giving reviews, I normally just rant on forever, I am going to make a list describing the book.<br><br>1.	Heart on a chain is about Kate, a girl whose mother beats her, her father is practically un-aware (I’m sure he knows what’s going on but he does nothing to stop it). So, Kate has spent the last 6 years of high school and middle school being the laughing stock of the schools. Because she is poor, does not defend herself and because they can. This all starts to change when her old friend Henry moves back to town. Henry use to be Kate's best friend and maybe for a little while something more. Henry comes back to this girl who is a shell of the girl he knew. Over time they become friends and then when everything is settling down, maybe something more.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380359110i/710273.jpg" width="313" height="400" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>2.	So, it had a good plot and there were enough twists and turns to keep you interested (so much that I was thoroughly shocked at some parts of the book), I have never before read a book with any resemblance to a plot like this. It was original and interesting and I stayed up (not studying for a test) to read this (totally worth it)!<br><br>3.	Now onto the characters, the author wrote the characters so well, there were some that you wanted to hate because of what they did and then you see their past and you learn why they are like that, lot’s of mixed emotions. There were a few characters (especially the main ones) that you just instantly loved; they had normal flaws, flaws that us as humans (and some aliens) have too. Yes, there were parts of the book where I wanted to slap Kate for being such an idiot (I refrained myself). But that’s what a good book has. It has us so emotionally vested in a character that we want to do that. This book sure has a lot of that.<br><br>This book is a great read, and I recommend it to anyone looking for a good read, it may be out of your usual genre of books but give it a go, with the beautifully written characters and story, you may be pleasantly surprised.<br></span>
  <a data-text-id="9434323796834926419" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

This was book love for me.</span>

Bennett' rel='nofollow noopener'>Heart on a Chain</a> is as heart-wrenching, gut-clenching and tear-jerking as it gets. I devoured this in almost no time; ending up a sobbing mess more than just once. Kate’s fate is awful and her story painful to read but on the other hand there are a lot of beautiful moments and Henry truly is an angel. I really enjoyed this, even if the story got a little overdramatic at times but altogether I’m glad I’ve read this.</span>

<div id="review_231297721" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/231297721" />
    <a title="Kelli" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4648687-kelli"><img alt="Kelli" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1338175152p2/4648687.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/231297721?book_show_action=true">Nov 04, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kelli" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kelli" href="/user/show/4648687-kelli">Kelli</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Nook 2940012700216" href="/book/show/10331995-heart-on-a-chain">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4648687-kelli?shelf=main-character-must-be-medicated">main-character-must-be-medicated</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4648687-kelli?shelf=i-just-can-t">i-just-can-t</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer231297721&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer231297721" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3691605183529047431">My apologies to the author, because she has accomplished more than I ever will just by publishing a book. And it takes a lot of guts to put yourself out there. I really had high hopes for this book from all of the glowing reviews, and normally I love a good, angsty love story, but this? I couldn't even finish. <br/><br/>This story is just trying too hard at everything. This Poor Girl's life is HORRIBLE. I get it. And the Hero Who Rides Back Into Town to Save Her is AMAZING. And the Poor Girl's mother and </span>
  <span id="freeText3691605183529047431" style="display:none">My apologies to the author, because she has accomplished more than I ever will just by publishing a book. And it takes a lot of guts to put yourself out there. I really had high hopes for this book from all of the glowing reviews, and normally I love a good, angsty love story, but this? I couldn't even finish. <br /><br />This story is just trying too hard at everything. This Poor Girl's life is HORRIBLE. I get it. And the Hero Who Rides Back Into Town to Save Her is AMAZING. And the Poor Girl's mother and father are EVIL. And the Hero's family is WONDERFUL. I. Get. It.<br /><br />Abuse in any form is terrible, and it happens everywhere, everyday to way too many good and innocent people (and animals). But what happened to Kate in this book, it just felt like TOO MUCH. Like, let's imagine every possible horrible thing that can happen and then add more horrible things to it. Everyone, everywhere, beats up on this girl, until magically an old childhood crush moves back and rescues her (after much drama and angst and horribleness to make Kate look even more pathetic and Henry even more wonderful). Subtle, this story is not.<br /><br />I also could just tell Kate was going to kill her mother in self-defense at some point. And that too just felt again like the book was trying too hard to shock me, that that plot point was used to add to the angst and make Kate even more a mess for Henry to clean up.<br /><br />I stopped reading after she killed her mother, so in all fairness, this book could've redeemed itself by the end. Possibly. But I couldn't make it that far. I REALLY tried. I just...couldn't. <br /><br />The glaring grammatical errors also did not further the case for me to finish this book. That was the only thing I did feel like crying about while reading Heart on a Chain.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3691605183529047431" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_456884733" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/456884733" />
    <a title="❀ Crystal ✿ -  PEACE ☮ LOVE ♥ BOOKS " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10734393-crystal---peace-love-books"><img alt="❀ Crystal ✿ -  PEACE ☮ LOVE ♥ BOOKS " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1396916584p2/10734393.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/456884733?book_show_action=true">Nov 15, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="❀ Crystal ✿ -  PEACE ☮ LOVE ♥ BOOKS " class="user" itemprop="url" name="❀ Crystal ✿ -  PEACE ☮ LOVE ♥ BOOKS " href="/user/show/10734393-crystal---peace-love-books">❀ Crystal ✿ -  PEACE ☮ LOVE ♥ BOOKS </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10734393-crystal---peace-love-books?shelf=2013-read-list">2013-read-list</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10734393-crystal---peace-love-books?shelf=re-read">re-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10734393-crystal---peace-love-books?shelf=best-ever">best-ever</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10734393-crystal---peace-love-books?shelf=2014-read-list">2014-read-list</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer456884733" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer713902580149045787">Hands down <b>Heart on a Chain</b> is one of my all time favorite books EVER. I can’t believe this book is not more popular than it is because it will grip you from the start and you won’t want to be freed. Your emotions will be all over the place combined with feelings of love, passion and absolute hatred for the pain the main character is suffering. Where some might call this book overly sweet, which at times it is, the overall dynamic and progression of character development trumps any and all bad, </span>
  <span id="freeText713902580149045787" style="display:none">Hands down <b>Heart on a Chain</b> is one of my all time favorite books EVER. I can’t believe this book is not more popular than it is because it will grip you from the start and you won’t want to be freed. Your emotions will be all over the place combined with feelings of love, passion and absolute hatred for the pain the main character is suffering. Where some might call this book overly sweet, which at times it is, the overall dynamic and progression of character development trumps any and all bad, at least in my opinion. <br /><br />So I don’t know why but I’m a sucker for any type of damsel in distress/ abusive situations. Even though this book is YA, much of the drama is more adult in nature and the overwhelming feelings of hate towards Kate’s mother make it appear more Adult in nature. Those who are easily turned off by any type of abuse, I warn you to steer clear, because there are some very graphic scenes in the book which could be hard to read. <br /><br />Since she was a young girl, Kate has been on her own. Not that she lives alone or anything, more like her parents checked out. Her mother is a stay at home alcoholic whose every breath is used to torment Kate and when the mood strikes she takes out her pain and suffering on her underage daughter, often using her fists or anything else she can find. Kate’s mother is truly evil. Some crucial part of her humanity has been wiped away and Kate is left to suffer the brunt of her mother’s wrath. <br /><br />As a young girl Kate met Henry and she loved him even then. When Henry moved away the light in Kate’s world went out. Growing up was hard on her own and the other kids never made it easy on her. Where her home life sucked, her school life was an easy comparison with all the bullies making Kate’s life even more unbearable. She’s teased, beat up on and has had many questionable substances dumped on her in the lunch room. <br /><br />The last thing Kate expects is for Henry to return. Even more than that she can’t imagine this grown up version of Henry would want anything to do with her. Surely the other kids would make sure of that. Henry is one determined boy and he remembers Kate clearly. In fact he has never forgotten her. Returning to his old school and reconnecting with Kate is something Henry never thought would happen. He couldn’t be happier. That is until he sees how everyone treats her. To say Henry is angered is a huge understatement. Not a violent person himself, Henry can’t understand how anyone could be so cruel, especially to someone like his Kate. <br /><br />I could go on and on about how beautiful this book is. It wouldn’t be a lie either. From the abuse to the romance every page is a reading delight. It’s too bad there is not more written by this author. I have easily read this book 5 times if not more and I know I will continue to read it many more times in the future. There’s just something about it that will suck you in and charge your emotions to revolve around these characters and everything that is happening. I wish there were more books written this well about such a touchy subject matter that still manages to catch the heart and soul of the reader. Unfortunately there is not much more out there from this author but I will continue to love, appreciate and share this book until the universe (if possible) finds something better.<br /><br />*****************************************<br /><br />Edit..... Review Re-Read Sept. 1 2019<br />Every damn time I read this book, it hits me right in the feels. My stomach is still twisted with nerves and my heart is overheating and full from the sweetness. This is an absolutely remarkable YA read and unfortunately many of the topics are relatable and life like. Since she was young, Kate has lived in a house of demons. An alcoholic absentee father and an abusive, bitter drug addicted mother shadow her home life and bullies torment her days. Nowhere is safe for Kate and she basically lives in constant fear. The slightest moves make her flinch and self confidence is something not even existent in her life. Henry was one bright point in her life until he moved away when they were in grade school. When he returns poor Kate has so much fear and anxiety just from his presence and the belief that he returned and will be cruel to her is heartbreaking. Every situation is negatively evaluated and for most of her young life unfortunately simply waking up for a new day is a guarantee of pain. Henry, sweet Henry is one of those impossible to believe guys. He stands up for the little guy, defends Kate when he doesn’t even know the situation or her past and really worked hard to earn her trust. I can completely understand Keyes hesitancy too, Henry is almost too good to be true but he’s everything Kate didn’t know she needed. Kate’s victim mentality life was hard to witness, forgiving the unforgivable and even trying to reforge mangled relationships is the only issue I have with the book. Kate like Henry, is almost too good and nice to be real. Her circumstance is sadly common in many ways and yet Kate seemed to almost too quickly begin to trust again and pass along forgiveness. No one would blame her for holding on to her feelings and I guess because personally I don’t think I could forgive what some people have done to her I don’t get it. There is a reason this is a common reread for me and will probably be for years. It’s phenomenal and while overly sweet and toothache inducing it’s also a beautifully woven story about a young girl who lives a life in hell until her long lost childhood love and guardian angel returns to steal both her heart and mine. Simply amazing 😍</span>
  <a data-text-id="713902580149045787" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_162320046" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/162320046" />
    <a title="Sandy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4515165-sandy"><img alt="Sandy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1320017147p2/4515165.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/162320046?book_show_action=true">Apr 20, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sandy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sandy" href="/user/show/4515165-sandy">Sandy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4515165-sandy?shelf=endings-i-love">endings-i-love</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4515165-sandy?shelf=can-t-stop-thinking-about">can-t-stop-thinking-about</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4515165-sandy?shelf=chemistry-sigh">chemistry-sigh</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4515165-sandy?shelf=i-own">i-own</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4515165-sandy?shelf=read-in-2011">read-in-2011</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4515165-sandy?shelf=made-me-cry">made-me-cry</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer162320046" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14948453714930590169">Cindy C. Bennett, you know how to make me cry. I'm not much of a book crier, but you've made me weep through not just one book, but TWO. You have some magic button that just unleashes my tear ducts so that I find myself sobbing while reading. And then, you add these crazy-good, awwww endings that make me smile through my tears. May we have some more, please?<br/><br/>I devoured Cindy's book <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/8883501.Geek_Girl' title='Geek Girl by Cindy C. Bennett' rel='nofollow noopener'>Geek Girl</a> and couldn't stop thinking about it. Her writing and characters draw me in and make me feel like I'm prese</span>
  <span id="freeText14948453714930590169" style="display:none">Cindy C. Bennett, you know how to make me cry. I'm not much of a book crier, but you've made me weep through not just one book, but TWO. You have some magic button that just unleashes my tear ducts so that I find myself sobbing while reading. And then, you add these crazy-good, awwww endings that make me smile through my tears. May we have some more, please?<br /><br />I devoured Cindy's book <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/8883501.Geek_Girl" title="Geek Girl by Cindy C. Bennett" rel="nofollow noopener">Geek Girl</a> and couldn't stop thinking about it. Her writing and characters draw me in and make me feel like I'm present for everything--that I'm watching my best friend live these events. I have now read BOTH of Cindy's books in one sitting each because I care so much about these characters that I can't stop without knowing the conclusion of their story.<br /><br />While <i>Geek Girl</i> is a little lighter, a littler fluffier, <i>Heart on a Chain</i> tackles some serious issues: abuse and bullying. You can't read this book without it making you want to be a nicer, better person. It exposes the effects of bullying in a way that tore at my heart. It showed how a plea for help may be stifled or go unnoticed because bullying has isolated and destroyed someone to the point where there's no one she can trust to protect her from unimaginable horrors at home. A particular conversation between Kate and a tormentor at the end had me WEEPING as the tormentor realized what her bullying had done--how she had made sure Kate had no friends...and thus no one to confide her terrible secret to.<br /><br /><b>Every mean girl needs to read this book.</b><br /><br />Bad boys, move aside. Cindy sure knows how to write the white knight. Her heroes are squeaky clean and devoted, and it's refreshing to see the anti-jerk get some page time. Cindy's boys are so...non-judgy. Henry and Kate share some sweet chemistry, and Henry's epilogue at the end had me awwwwing because it was so adorable. (Yes, Henry, ADORABLE.) <br /><br />While the events may border a tiny bit on melodramatic at times, <i>Heart on a Chain</i> made me want to stamp out bullying and sprinkle friendship and kind words all around. I can't think of a better way to teach teenagers the effects of bullying. This is a story of abuse, redeeming love, and forgiveness that's unforgettable.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14948453714930590169" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer6700498019702433451">Not a review. Just a reminder<br/>From <br/><br/>Nov 15, 2011 Alex<br/><br/><br/><a class='jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction'>(view spoiler)</a><span class='spoilerContainer' style='display: none'>[Ale** spoiler alert ** What the fuck? I cannot understand how people are giving it 5-star reviews because this was one of the worst things I've ever read.<br/><br/>I couldn't believe the whole book was so black and white. Kate, a victim of horrible abuse at the hands of her mother, has been ridiculed by her peers for her appearance for years. In fact, they physically abuse her too (wtf that scene)! But her knight on a white horse comes to h</span></span>
  <span id="freeText6700498019702433451" style="display:none">Not a review. Just a reminder<br />From <br /><br />Nov 15, 2011 Alex<br /><br /><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Ale** spoiler alert ** What the fuck? I cannot understand how people are giving it 5-star reviews because this was one of the worst things I've ever read.<br /><br />I couldn't believe the whole book was so black and white. Kate, a victim of horrible abuse at the hands of her mother, has been ridiculed by her peers for her appearance for years. In fact, they physically abuse her too (wtf that scene)! But her knight on a white horse comes to her rescue in the form of Henry, her friend from childhood who has recently moved back to town. Henry is The Perfect Man. He's rich, kind, generous, and has loved Kate ever since they were little...even though he moved away.<br /><br />Henry finds Kate irresistible. In fact, we are told that Kate's beauty is what her peers, especially the girls, hate about her. It Cannot Be Diminished By Her Circumstances. Henry has no problem getting Kate to fall in love with him, though she refuses to tell him about her home life. Which, in all fairness, is really really horrible.<br /><br />But the whole thing was gross. Kate had no autonomy. Henry saved her. He swooped in and literally is her salvation. She isn't able to do anything without him. Also, everyone loves Kate. Everyone who matters, that is. Which is Henry and his whole wonderful family. THEY LOVE HER IMMEDIATELY. THEY ARE THE PERFECT FAMILY. HIS MOTHER MAKES PUMPKIN SOUP AND SERVES IT IN HOLLOW PUMPKINS. HIS GRANDFATHER GIVES HER $1000 SIMPLY BECAUSE HE CAN SEE THAT SHE IS HENRY'S SOULMATE.<br /><br />And why? I don't know. Kate is always telling herself that she doesn't deserve him and he's too good for her and, well, he's her only friend. GROSS. This story could have totally set Kate up as an awesome female protagonist, doing the best despite her circumstances, and using her own tools to love Henry AND to escape her abuse, but instead it's Henry who does everything for her. I mean, don't men always?<br /><br />Henry even proposes at the end, even though they're 17. I don't know what 13-year-old wrote this book, but it was atrocious. It's some pathetic fantasy concocted out of soap opera-worthy melodrama, written by a woman who clearly believes that only men can save battered women. I had trouble believing that this book actually existed and that I was reading it. But, you know, why shouldn't it be? Millions of idiots love Twilight; why shouldn't they also love this piece of trash?<br /><br />EDIT: The more I think about this book, the more upset I am. I actually think this is one of those novels doing a disservice to young women living with domestic violence because it tells them that only a man can come save them. This will make it far more likely for these young women to go from one abusive situation into another one, becoming emotionally dependent on their "savior", and unable to develop their independence. For example, Kate, who leaves her mother only to go to Henry.<br /><br />(Let's not even go into Kate's mother's depression and mental illness, which is an incredibly sad story in itself...)<br /><br />This isn't to say that Henry isn't a paragon of virtue, because apparently he's the Greatest Dude Ever. Which is awesome for Kate and all, since that really could've ended poorly. But Bennett could have easily EASILY made Kate the hero of her own story. I know I'm getting all rah-rah feminist (WHICH I HAPPEN TO THINK IS GREAT), but honestly, I saw this kind of stuff every day with my young female clients. <br /><br />That being said, this thing was just crock full of shit. I apparently forgot to address the part where the Mean Girl bully beats the crap out of Kate at school. Like, physically, on the floor of the girls' bathroom, beats the crap out of her. It's needlessly violent and gratuitous. But once the truth about Kate's home life is revealed, suddenly the bully is all apologetic and weepy. Like, "SORRY FOR BEATING YOU UP. I THOUGHT YOU WERE ALL GROSS AND SMELLY AND STUFF. I TOTES WOULDN'T HAVE DONE THAT IF I KNEW YOU WERE GETTING BEATEN ON AT HOME. MY B." And Kate's all, "NBD, girl, I got you."<br /><br />YEAH.<br /><br />THAT HAPPENS.<br /><br />AND THEN THEY BECOME FRIENDS.<br /><br />So...what's the message I'm getting here? That it was okay for her to beat Kate up had Kate NOT been from an abusive home? Or, maybe, and I'm going out on a limb here, Bennett could have made it clear that such bullying and violence is abhorrent under ANY circumstance. I'm not saying that Bennett was condoning the physical and emotional bullying by justifying it like that. I'm saying that was how it read in the book and I just wish that Jessica (was that her name?) could have undergone her own transformation in a different way as well.<br /><br />In conclusion: if you're a sane person with rational ideas about how people should treat each other and you like strong female characters, you're probs going to want to throw your ebook reader against the wall. I wish I could give this NEGATIVE STARS. I know I shouldn't expect YA authors to be role models, BUT THEY ARE, because youth read their books and are influenced by them and TAKE THEM TO HEART. And that's why books like this and Twilight INFURIATE me. At least Henry doesn't creep into Kate's bedroom to watch her sleep. We should be telling young women that THEY ARE STRONG AND THEY ARE THE PROTAGONISTS OF THEIR OWN STORY AND THEY SHOULD NEVER UNDERESTIMATE THEMSELVES. We should never, ever tell them that they can only be someone in relation to someone else. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="6700498019702433451" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Anesha †Curious &amp; Obsessive Bookworm†" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Anesha †Curious &amp; Obsessive Bookworm†" href="/user/show/7020250-anesha-curious-obsessive-bookworm">Anesha †Curious &amp; Obsessive Bookworm†</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7020250-anesha-curious-obsessive-bookworm?shelf=abuse">abuse</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer241328647" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer4162256781532232612"><i>As his mouth comes down to mines, my heart lifts free of its burden and soars.<br/>I'm back where I belong</i><br/><br/><b>5 STAR HEARTS~~!!!</b><br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380364051ra/715564.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>It gets me so giddy just thinking about it. And gosh dangit don't I love a book that leaves me all fuzzy and warm? Sends me on a roller-coaster, demanding I experience such a simple yet powerful read?<br/><br/><i>This book gone and done it</i><br/><br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380364051ra/715565.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>We enter Kate, who's life is like living <i>hell</i>. <br/>All Kate wants to do is be invisible. Get through high school and away from the bullying she's subjected to </span>
  <span id="freeText4162256781532232612" style="display:none"><i>As his mouth comes down to mines, my heart lifts free of its burden and soars.<br>I'm back where I belong</i><br><br><b>5 STAR HEARTS~~!!!</b><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380364051ra/715564.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>It gets me so giddy just thinking about it. And gosh dangit don't I love a book that leaves me all fuzzy and warm? Sends me on a roller-coaster, demanding I experience such a simple yet powerful read?<br><br><i>This book gone and done it</i><br><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380364051ra/715565.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>We enter Kate, who's life is like living <i>hell</i>. <br>All Kate wants to do is be invisible. Get through high school and away from the bullying she's subjected to within those walls. Hopes that she can get by another day at home without her mother hitting her... She's constantly walking on thin ice it seems, wondering when the cold will swallow her and numb her completely.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380364051i/715566.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I feel stupid, because just thinking about this beautiful book is making me emotional xD.<br><br>Kate is truly a beautifully strong minded person. She went through so much - more than anyone should ever have to go through. On top of that, she still worked towards pleasing her mom, still remember the past - right down to the very day before all went wrong so many years ago. <br><br>The emotions in this book seemed almost tangible. The author did a wonderful job in portraying it, helping me to connect with each and everyone of those characters - even the bad ones. She explained things fully, gave an example for the actions, the reasons behind them. I loved that the most, especially given my last read. xD So to have that poured out towards me across those pages were wonderful. It left me emotionally wrecked. I remember reading it at work yesterday and just silently crying like an idiot. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380364051ra/715567.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>The silver lining in all that grey was when Henry was re-introduced. They'd had an innocent relationship back in grade school I think, but sadly he moved away.<br><br>Upon his arrival, meeting up with her - not once did he shun her. I love that she was still apprehensive of his kindness. She was so messed up over the years that her trust for anyone was completely gone - Even for the boy who got her first and only kiss. He always greeted her - even when she refused to answer him... and he sat with her, never caring that others openly shunned her. Henry was a guy who didn't care what others said or do - he'd do what he saw fit without care. And trying to befriend Kate once more was something he was adamant about.<br><br>Can I just say - him being a lefty makes him like, a bazillion times hotter? haha... I'm a lefty too and the little detail just to say he's a lefty (and he turns his book like me when writing?) just made me feel closer to him! lol. Yh shut up - am stooopidly in love :P<br><br><b>
  <i>"I want to be your friend," he says and my stomach tightens.<br>"You can't be my friend. No one can be my friend. It's social suicide."<br>He reaches out and brushes his fingers lightly over the bandage knotted on my hand, leaving an improbable trail of fire. "I can honestly say that even if that is true, I don't care."</i>
</b><br><br>I love how she always ran from him, or avoided him. His actions just kept her on edge and it was funny at times. Especially the scene where he literally had to chase her! lol<br><br><br>Henry is just so damn amazing. He's popular, doesn't follow the crowd...He's like... EVERYTHING a girl could ever ask for! He's a perfect gentleman! I mean <i>he opens car doors</i>.... <br><br>Doing things like that? There's no second thought to my final answer;<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380222758ra/501737.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><br>Both Henry and Kate are selfless and the love that gradually grew between them were so rewarding to read....<br><br>OMG... why do I keep trying to write rational reviews!<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380222758ra/496693.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>This book is freakin' amazing!! It not only show the abused life of Kate, it drags you along for the ride, making you experience <i>everything</i> this book has to offer. You'll cry, you'll laugh, have that idiotic smile on your face at times. It's gonna hurt reading certain parts, your throat with dry out, the constriction on your heart will be unbearable.<br><br>Tears will blur your vision.<br><br><i>But it'll all be worth it.</i> <br><br>I finished this book with a happy sigh. It was a bittersweet departure but I'm really happy I finally got to read it.<br><br>I absolutely love how everyone gradually accepted her, which only makes Henry that much more amazing. He was subtle but he was adamant. And I loved him for that. He was mature far beyond his age... Omg and the scene of their 2nd kiss (1st since his return) was too amazing. I had this shit eating grin on my face.<br><br>And it literally felt like my heart had grown wings, threatening to fly away into the safety of Henry... Someone please tell my heart Henry is just fictional?!?!<br><br><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[But don't try convincing my mind!! :D<a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[<br><br><span>[image error]</span><br><br><br><br> <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>

<div id="review_395362356" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/395362356" />
    <a title="Aestas Book Blog" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5604583-aestas-book-blog"><img alt="Aestas Book Blog" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1353371225p2/5604583.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/395362356?book_show_action=true">Aug 19, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Aestas Book Blog" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Aestas Book Blog" href="/user/show/5604583-aestas-book-blog">Aestas Book Blog</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer395362356" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13936285895395659569"><b> A YA story about surviving child abuse, about learning that everyone is worthy of love, and about the strength of forgiveness. </b><br/><br/>Henry grew up in school with Kate. He fell in love with her on the first day of kindergarten when she befriended him, and with a big smile, made him feel welcome and since then they became best friends. Until, one summer, his family moved away.<br/><br/>Six years later, its the senior year of high school. With an alcoholic father who is too drunk to notice that her prescrition-dr</span>
  <span id="freeText13936285895395659569" style="display:none"><b> A YA story about surviving child abuse, about learning that everyone is worthy of love, and about the strength of forgiveness. </b><br><br>Henry grew up in school with Kate. He fell in love with her on the first day of kindergarten when she befriended him, and with a big smile, made him feel welcome and since then they became best friends. Until, one summer, his family moved away.<br><br>Six years later, its the senior year of high school. With an alcoholic father who is too drunk to notice that her prescrition-drug-addicted mother regularly beats and abuses her at home, and her thrift store clothes making her the target of severe and relentless bullying at school, Kate is a the subject of horrific treatment everywhere she turns. Consequently, she has withdrawn into herself, a survival mechanisn against a world where no where is safe.<br><br>When she walks into school on the first day back and sees Henry standing there, she is shocked and mortified that he'll see what she's becomes. Henry, however, is the same kind, caring, tender and gentle yet protective guy he always was. He's surprised at the change in her, and does his best to earn her trust. And throughout the book we see her journey as Henry helps her heal, learn to stand up for herself, and begin to truly believe she is worthy of love.<br><br>I loved Henry's character - what an absolute sweetheart! He was the first person to show her kindness after so many years of being shunned, abused and bullied, the first person to stand up for her, to protect her, to care for her feelings, and to love her. He was utterly devoted to her from start to finish and watching him gently lead her out of her shell by wrapping her in his love and love from his family was really beautiful.<br><br><i> "I'm sorry," he says, sincerity in ever line of his body and ringing in his voice. "I'm sorry you had to go through all of that alone. I'm sorry for everything you are going through now. But I promise you one thing." He leans back, taking my face between his hands and gazing intently into my eyes. "You will never be alone again." </i><br><br>The physical abuse the Kate suffers at home is horrific and chilling. Pure, downright cruelty. And almost worse than that is seeing how she internalizes the pain and feels unworthy - if her own mother can't love her, how can she be deserving of any love at all? It was just heart breaking to see such a sweet, shy, kind person be treated so brutally.<br><br>Throughout the book, we get to see the back story behind the abuse - why was Kate's mom so bitter? What made her dad so detached? And we got to see the new beginnings brought about from acceptance and forgiveness.<br><br>I liked the book, but I didn't love it despite having no specific complaints about it. It was pretty short, I read it in less than a day. The whole feeling of the book was very quiet... I know that's a bit of a weird way to describe a book, but that's how it felt to me. The story progressed at an unrushed pace, never making you feel like you missed any part of the story.....but I don't know, I guess despite liking the story, I just felt a little detached from it. It did almost make me misty eyed once or twice, but it didn't rip out my heart or make me cry ever despite the subject matter being pretty sickening at times. Still, it is a good read, and definitely worth adding to the TBR list.<br><br>The whole story is told from Kate's POV, except for the prologue and epilogue which is told from Henry's POV. And yes, the story does have a happy ending :)<br><br>It was definitely YA... very light and non-steamy (just kisses), but very sweet.<br><br>And someone asked me about this so I'll mention that there is no sexual abuse in this story.<br><br>Henry and Kate casting:<br><br><span>[image error]</span><br><br><img width="100%" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380388227i/748610._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>For more of my reviews, visit <a href="http://aestasbookblog.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Aestas Book Blog</a><br><br>And come join the Aestas Book Blog <a href="http://www.facebook.com/pages/Aestas-Book-Blog/332404836826905" rel="nofollow noopener"> Facebook Page</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="13936285895395659569" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_256788817" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/256788817" />
    <a title="Alexis *Reality Bites*" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5587514-alexis-reality-bites"><img alt="Alexis *Reality Bites*" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1404308282p2/5587514.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/256788817?book_show_action=true">Jan 05, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

<span id="freeTextContainer14624513194950422202">Spoiler Free Review<br/>5 STAR READ<br/>Genre: YA Romance<br/> <b>Warning</b>- the subject matter in this book is very raw. If you can not handle reading a book with child abuse i would not suggest you read this book.<br/><br/>Heart on a chain is about about a young girl named Kate entering her senior year of high school. Kate's mom is a pill popper and her dad is an alcholic. Home is no fun; dad beats mom, mom beats Kate. And it's not only at home does Kate suffer but at school she is bullied by both the male and female stude</span>
  <span id="freeText14624513194950422202" style="display:none">Spoiler Free Review<br />5 STAR READ<br />Genre: YA Romance<br /> <b>Warning</b>- the subject matter in this book is very raw. If you can not handle reading a book with child abuse i would not suggest you read this book.<br /><br />Heart on a chain is about about a young girl named Kate entering her senior year of high school. Kate's mom is a pill popper and her dad is an alcholic. Home is no fun; dad beats mom, mom beats Kate. And it's not only at home does Kate suffer but at school she is bullied by both the male and female students. On the first day of school Kate see's Henry a childhood friend, Henry wants to befriend Kate again. But because of all the trauma she has endured from other students it takes Kate a while to see that Henry is genuine. <br /><br />Eventually love blossoms btwn the two. Kate get's a chance to see what a family should be when she visits Henry's house. His loving mother, father and sisters all embrace Kate lovingly. But at home the drama and abuse only escalates and becomes a life or death situation. Leaving Kate to fight for her life. <br /><br /><u>Thoughts</u><br />This story was written very well it is an intense ride that shows how a traumatic loss can change a person into someone else completely different. Kate's mom was not always bitter and mean and her father was not always detached. Circumstances lead to their change leaving Kate a victim to their on going crimes as bad parents.<br /><br /><u>Thoughts on Characters</u><br />-Kate is a very shy girl with very very low self esteem. She does not believe she deserves much in life and it projects from her thoughts to her life she does not realize that she can be and do amazing things. I spent most of the book pitying her. Her dad is an asshole and her mom is an even bigger asshole.<br /><br />-Henry is the man and he makes you wish your high school boyfriend could of been just like him!<br /><br />My Ratings<br />Characters- Lovable<br />Writing style- Excellent and very Honest<br />Plot/Storyline- Intense and Raw<br />Steam Factor- Moderate<br />Overall- A Very Goodread!!</span>

<div id="review_178199224" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/178199224" />
    <a title="ILoveBooks" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4177633-ilovebooks"><img alt="ILoveBooks" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1490728067p2/4177633.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/178199224?book_show_action=true">Jun 20, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="ILoveBooks" class="user" itemprop="url" name="ILoveBooks" href="/user/show/4177633-ilovebooks">ILoveBooks</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781456492410" href="/book/show/10331991-heart-on-a-chain">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer178199224" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3576129558065119132">Never judge a girl by her cover. The main character, Kate, has lived with abuse her whole life. She is very resilient and strong, wonderful qualities to see in a female character. She deals with her alcoholic father and drug-addicted mother on a regular basis, sometimes coming out the worse for wear. Some might see her refusal to stand up for herself as a shame and weak, and it might be; however, Kate is also a proud character, possibly a bad trait in this situation, but it works as a character </span>
  <span id="freeText3576129558065119132" style="display:none">Never judge a girl by her cover. The main character, Kate, has lived with abuse her whole life. She is very resilient and strong, wonderful qualities to see in a female character. She deals with her alcoholic father and drug-addicted mother on a regular basis, sometimes coming out the worse for wear. Some might see her refusal to stand up for herself as a shame and weak, and it might be; however, Kate is also a proud character, possibly a bad trait in this situation, but it works as a character should never be perfect. <br /><br /><br /><br />The novel contains several scenes with severe abuse and bullying. This is a reality for some teens. The author makes these scenes both vivid and real for the reader. The reader will want to reach out to help Kate while smacking her mother. The love interest, Henry, comes in the nick of time for Kate. He is caring, protective, and appears to truly love Kate. He is also rich; the opposite of what Kate is acclimated too. The reader will enjoy watching as their relationship deepens and develops. <br /><br /><br /><br />This novel will make the reader want to hunt down every mean girl and bad parent in the world and give them what for. Incidentally, the author is very good to evoke that sort of reaction in her readers. The dialogue is interesting and horrifying at times, but the reader can believe this is actually happening. The scene, with an alcoholic father and drug-addicted mother, is perfect. Kate's second-hand clothing and the way she is bullied at school will make this novel all to real to the reader. There are good transitions from one scene to the next and the author manages to give Kate the perfect reactions to the situations she is placed in-Kate reacts like a textbook would predict with some surprises, again she is believable. The ending is very satisfying and the reader will breathe a sigh of relief. This novel is recommended for young adults/adults who enjoy novels that tackle real life issues. <br /><br /><br /><br />5 Stars<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="3576129558065119132" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1777400874" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1777400874" />
    <a title="Sky" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/32831460-sky"><img alt="Sky" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1590554430p2/32831460.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1777400874?book_show_action=true">Oct 06, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sky" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sky" href="/user/show/32831460-sky">Sky</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32831460-sky?shelf=could-not-finish">could-not-finish</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1777400874" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16003366246395859713"><br/>In all honesty, I am sick of these types of books, books that use abuse as a plot devices to trigger sympathy, but all its triggering is anger. This book is shallow, mediocre and an even worse replica of <i>Barely Breathing</i>, there were a lot of grammar mistakes, a lot of unnecessary scenes and a hell of a lot of scenes that are supposed to be heart-breaking, but all it got out of me is an eye-roll. <br/><br/>Kate, our perfect MC, is beautiful, so beautiful that all the girls are jealous of her and beat her u</span>
  <span id="freeText16003366246395859713" style="display:none"><br />In all honesty, I am sick of these types of books, books that use abuse as a plot devices to trigger sympathy, but all its triggering is anger. This book is shallow, mediocre and an even worse replica of <i>Barely Breathing</i>, there were a lot of grammar mistakes, a lot of unnecessary scenes and a hell of a lot of scenes that are supposed to be heart-breaking, but all it got out of me is an eye-roll. <br /><br />Kate, our perfect MC, is beautiful, so beautiful that all the girls are jealous of her and beat her up in bathrooms, so perfect that her mother beats her up to let out some steam. I know abuse exists, and I am 176% against it, I just disagree with the way the author portrayed it. <br /><br />There was this troll account I was following on twitter Junior year high school that was trolling online fan fiction authors that always describe a beautiful girl followed by “I’m so ugly”, although I understand insecurities exist, I don’t understand why authors love to make them so exotically beautiful whilst believing they look like a grinch.<br />I’ll share a quote below and you’ll be the judge:<br /><br /><i>“With a finger, I trace smooth skin (blessed with acne free, blemish free complexion), straight nose, eyebrows neither too bushy nor thin, an ordinary mouth, indented chin. I suppose my eyes are my best feature, wide and fringed with dark lashes. They’re light blue, ringed with gold.<br /><br />I shake my head and let my hair fall back into place. Nothing attractive, extraordinarily plain, but he still wants to be my friend”</i><br /><br />All in all, I personally won’t recommend this, but opinions differ, so don’t let my opinion be the reason you avoided this. <br /></span>

          </span>

<div id="review_219051761" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/219051761" />
    <a title="Michelle [Helen Geek]" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5557851-michelle-helen-geek"><img alt="Michelle [Helen Geek]" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1448463806p2/5557851.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/219051761?book_show_action=true">Oct 04, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Michelle [Helen Geek]" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Michelle [Helen Geek]" href="/user/show/5557851-michelle-helen-geek">Michelle [Helen Geek]</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5557851-michelle-helen-geek?shelf=4-5-stars">4-5-stars</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5557851-michelle-helen-geek?shelf=nook-tbr">nook-tbr</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5557851-michelle-helen-geek?shelf=gr-high-recommend">gr-high-recommend</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5557851-michelle-helen-geek?shelf=ya">ya</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer219051761" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8263246987316572587">Okay - I bit and I'm glad I did. This book was a GR recommendation for me based on books I've rated. It isn't typical for me to read a YA, so was skeptical, but I read the book blurb and thought about my kids and some of their freinds and decided to try it. Very glad I did.<br/><br/>The premise for this book is a childs courage in handling tragedy dealt by a parent. How the love of a freind can be comforting and redeeming. And, in the end, we can survive and come out on the other end, with the support of </span>
  <span id="freeText8263246987316572587" style="display:none">Okay - I bit and I'm glad I did. This book was a GR recommendation for me based on books I've rated. It isn't typical for me to read a YA, so was skeptical, but I read the book blurb and thought about my kids and some of their freinds and decided to try it. Very glad I did.<br /><br />The premise for this book is a childs courage in handling tragedy dealt by a parent. How the love of a freind can be comforting and redeeming. And, in the end, we can survive and come out on the other end, with the support of true friends.<br /><br />I give this book 4.5 stars. The only thing I had any difficulty swollowing, was the adult behavior in the book. Do I beleive a parent can terrorize a child - a huge yes. Do I think a child can walk through our lives and be invisible, sadly yes. Do I think adults will take a child who has been badly abused in, treat the injuries with love and tender care, then allow said child to go back into the environment, I highly doubt it. Another issue I had was with the parents of Henry. They knew this girl had issues, but they never discouraged the relationship - it would only get worse before it got better.<br /><br />Henry was the true hero of the book. He showed love and compassion throughout. His behavior was steller and anyone who has raised a son knows, he is what we strive to acheive. I know only fiction, but it truely touched something deep in me - as a parent and grandparent. I love this book.<br /><br />I would recommend it for anyone who loves a good story and believes with love, trust and compassion for our fellow man, we can be all be heroes.<br /><br />Happy Reading!</span>
  <a data-text-id="8263246987316572587" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

She is strong and brave, and has a great capacity to keep going and forgive.<br/><br/>Henry is the perfect guy that any girl in this world wants, it’s impossible to find fault to him. <tr class="no_border feedFooterReview" id="update_comment_stuff_Review1173518082">
  <td colspan="2">

<div id="review_155437138" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/155437138" />
    <a title="Vicki Keire" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4129072-vicki-keire"><img alt="Vicki Keire" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1303673489p2/4129072.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/155437138?book_show_action=true">Mar 19, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Vicki Keire" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Vicki Keire" href="/user/show/4129072-vicki-keire">Vicki Keire</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer155437138" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17203044464456357716">A remarkable piece of YA Indie fiction. This book was a bit out of my normal parameters, which lean a bit more towards the paranormal and dark fantasy, but it's been receiving rave reviews on Amazon. After reading Tabitha Suzuma's Forbidden, I've been eager to venture into some of the grittier realistic YA fiction. This novel is certainly that. I found myself in tears several times throughout the novel, and as much as I wanted to blame the novel for being over-the-top, the sad fact is that the s</span>
  <span id="freeText17203044464456357716" style="display:none">A remarkable piece of YA Indie fiction. This book was a bit out of my normal parameters, which lean a bit more towards the paranormal and dark fantasy, but it's been receiving rave reviews on Amazon. After reading Tabitha Suzuma's Forbidden, I've been eager to venture into some of the grittier realistic YA fiction. This novel is certainly that. I found myself in tears several times throughout the novel, and as much as I wanted to blame the novel for being over-the-top, the sad fact is that the situations depicted in the novel are all too real for many teens. Bennett shows remarkable prowess as a storyteller to take such a horrific story of abuse and tell it without coming across as hystrionic or over the top. Told in the first person, her protagonist goes through all the classic symptoms of abuse victims, and readers are with her as she changes over the course of the novel. The one thing I would like to have seen addressed is the Cinderella syndrome- yes, the protagonist does much of her own changing, but the fact remains that her rich and handsome boyfriend is the catalyst for most of it. Even this was fine with me. He was a great character, and so was his whole family, and I don't buy it that guys/people like him don't exist. I happen to be married to one. But whA remarkable piece of YA Indie fiction. This book was a bit out of my normal parameters, which lean a bit more towards the paranormal and dark fantasy, but it's been receiving rave reviews on Amazon. After reading Tabitha Suzuma's Forbidden, I've been eager to venture into some of the grittier realistic YA fiction. This novel is certainly that. I found myself in tears several times throughout the novel, and as much as I wanted to blame the novel for being over-the-top, the sad fact is that the situations depicted in the novel are all too real for many teens. Bennett shows remarkable prowess as a storyteller to take such a horrific story of abuse and tell it without coming across as hystrionic or over the top. Told in the first person, her protagonist goes through all the classic symptoms of abuse victims, and readers are with her as she changes over the course of the novel. The one thing I would like to have seen addressed is the Cinderella syndrome- yes, the protagonist does much of her own changing, but the fact remains that her rich and handsome boyfriend is the catalyst for most of it. Even this was fine with me. He was a great character, and so was his whole family, and I don't buy it that guys/people like him don't exist. I happen to be married to one. But what I would like to have seen was at least an internal examination of some kind about what would have happened if the boyfriend hadn't been there to rescue her. But this really was a fantastic read. It straddles the divide between YA and adult. Some younger readers may find the situations too disturbing, but some adults may, as well. But then, that's exactly why such stories must be told. But this really was a fantastic read. It straddles the divide between YA and adult. Some younger readers may find the situations too disturbing, but some adults may, as well. But then, that's exactly why such stories must be told.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer5258152865859063931">I read this in 2012 and all I remembered was that I liked it, so it was time for a re-read.<br/><br/>Kate is a 17 year old girl who's used to being bullied at school. People somehow feel that's she will never fight back, so she's an easy target. It doesn't help that she wears only second hand clothes and has no money whatsoever.<br/><br/>Kate learned at an early age that it's no use fighting bullies.
